вқҜ /competitive-landscape                                                        

вҸә Great context. The competitive landscape makes the positioning crystal clear вҖ”
   the team builder is the hub that connects everything that currently lives in
  separate tools. Key differentiators to keep in mind as we design:

  - рҹ“Ҡ Analytics-fed building вҖ” usage stats from Pikalytics/Munchstats baked
  right into the builder (not a separate tab)
  - рҹ”ў Inline damage calc вҖ” no context-switching to nerd-of-now
  - рҹӣЎпёҸ Type coverage matrix вҖ” what Gabby's builder does, but integrated
  - рҹ”Җ Team versioning/branching вҖ” iterate on teams, track what changed
  - рҹ‘Ҙ Collaborative editing + private sharing вҖ” beyond PokePaste's static links
  - вң… Format-aware validation вҖ” legality feedback as you build

  This is a big feature with a lot of surface area. Before I go further вҖ”

  How do you want to scope this brainstorm? Given the number of subsystems here
  (editor, analytics integration, damage calc, versioning,
  sharing/collaboration, type coverage), this might benefit from decomposition
  into phases:

  - A) Design the whole thing end-to-end in one spec вҖ” all subsystems together,
  so we have the full picture before building anything
  - B) Decompose into sub-projects now вҖ” identify the independent pieces, design
   the core editor first, then layer on analytics/damage calc/versioning/sharing
   as separate specs
  - C) Design the core builder experience thoroughly, but include "integration
  points" in the spec showing where analytics/damage calc/versioning plug in
  later вҖ” best of both worlds

  My instinct says C вҖ” it lets us go deep on the editor UX (the thing users will
   interact with most) while keeping the full vision documented. What do you
  think?

вқҜ /product-vision                                                               

вҸә This fills in the full picture. A few key things from the product vision that
  shape our design:

  Current state: Team Builder is already "Live" for basic team sheet
  parsing/validation/legality вҖ” integrated with tournament registration. What
  we're designing is the Analytics-Powered Team Builder upgrade (listed as
  "Coming Soon").

  The killer differentiator is team versioning/branching вҖ” "fork" a team, track
  how each version performed, see the full evolution history. This is what no
  competitor does. The builder isn't just an editor вҖ” it's a team laboratory
  with a paper trail.

  Four big subsystems emerge:
  1. рҹҸ—пёҸ Core editor вҖ” pick species, moves, abilities, items, EVs/IVs, tera type.
   Format validation. Import/export.
  2. рҹ”Җ Versioning & branching вҖ” fork teams, parent-child relationships,
  iteration history
  3. рҹ“Ҡ Analytics integration вҖ” trending picks, usage data, EV spreads fed into
  the builder
  4. рҹ‘Ҙ Collaboration & sharing вҖ” real-time co-editing (websockets), private
  sharing with revocable access, auto-expiry

  So back to my scoping question вҖ” given this is clearly a multi-system feature,
   how do you want to approach it?

  - A) One big end-to-end spec covering all four subsystems
  - B) Decompose now вҖ” design the core editor first, then layer the others as
  separate specs
  - C) Deep design on the core editor, with documented integration points for
  where analytics/versioning/collaboration plug in later

  I'm still leaning C вҖ” the core editor UX is the foundation everything else
  builds on, and getting that right matters most. But if you want the full
  vision documented first, A works too. What feels right?

  This is genuinely 6 interconnected subsystems. Given the scope, here's my next
   question:

  What's the user journey you envision? Specifically вҖ” when a user opens the
  team builder, what do they see first and how do they move through these
  systems? Pick the flow that feels most natural:

  - A) Editor-centric вҖ” You land on the team editor. Type analysis, meta data,
  and matchup planning are panels/tabs alongside it. Match tracker is accessed
  after saving.
  - B) Dashboard-centric вҖ” You land on a team "home" showing all your teams,
  their stats, recent matches. You click into a team to edit, analyze, or plan
  matchups.
  - C) Workspace-centric вҖ” The builder IS the workspace. Editor, analysis, meta,
   matchup planning, and match history are all views within a single persistent
  workspace per team. Like an IDE for Pokemon teams.

  This is a big system. So let me ask my scoping question one more time now that
   we have the full picture:

  Given these 7 subsystems, do you want to design the entire thing as one 
  unified spec, or decompose into phases? My recommendation is to design the
  core workspace layout + team editor + type analysis first (the foundation),
  with documented integration points for the other 4 systems. That gives us a
  buildable, useful V1 while keeping the full vision mapped. What do you think?

вҸә Liberty Note linked. Every entry in the competitive landscape now has a URL.

  Back to the brainstorm вҖ” I still have an open question for you. Given the 7
  subsystems we've identified, how do you want to scope this design?

  - A) One big end-to-end spec вҖ” all 7 systems designed together
  - B) Phase it вҖ” design the core editor first, layer others as separate specs
  - C) Deep design on core workspace + editor + type analysis, with documented
  integration points for the other 4 systems

  My recommendation is still C вҖ” it gets us a buildable, useful V1 while keeping
   the full vision mapped. What feels right to you?

вқҜ VGC Pastes is a great resources that tracks popular teams that good players   
  have built and gotten results with, we should incoporate that in as well      
вҸә Great call. VGC Pastes is already in the competitive landscape skill, but the
  key insight is that we should build team discovery directly into the builder вҖ”
   browse proven teams from top players, filter by format/archetype/placement,
  and one-click import into your workspace to fork and iterate on.

вҸә These are excellent ideas. Let me capture what you're describing because it's
  a core differentiator:

  Speed Tiers вҖ” context-aware:
  - No Pokemon selected: Show speed tiers scoped to your 6 team members vs the
  meta. "Your Rillaboom outspeeds their Amoonguss but is outsped by their
  Incineroar at this EV spread"
  - Pokemon selected: Zoom into just that Pokemon's speed tier вҖ” who do you
  outspeed, who outspeeds you, with common EV spreads from the meta. Noise
  reduced to what matters for this Pokemon.
  - Always expandable to the full tier list when you want the complete picture

  Damage Calculator вҖ” smart suggestions:
  - Instead of "enter attacker, defender, move" every time, the calc
  auto-suggests relevant calcs based on:
    - Your team's moves vs top meta threats ("Incineroar's Flare Blitz vs
  Rillaboom: 85-100%")
    - Common threats' attacks INTO your team ("Landorus-T Earthquake vs your
  Incineroar: 45-53%")
    - Matchups from the meta data вҖ” if Urshifu is popular, show calcs against it
   automatically
    - When you change an EV spread, live recalculate the suggested calcs so you
  see the impact immediately

  This is huge вҖ” it turns the damage calc from a manual tool into an ambient 
  intelligence layer. You don't go to the calc, the calc comes to you.

  Before I mock this up, did you have a preference on the left panel layout
  question? (Horizontal strip at top, vertical list on the side, or card grid?)
  Or should I just go with the horizontal strip since it's the most natural for

  these speed tier and smart calc ideas?

вҸә Yes вҖ” format-scoped filters on the species picker is a huge differentiator.
  Nobody else does this. Showdown gives you a flat list. Pikalytics gives you
  usage stats. But nobody lets you filter and discover Pokemon based on what's 
  actually happening in the meta for your specific format.

  Let me think through what filter categories would be most useful for a VGC
  player building a team in Reg I:

  Filters I can see being valuable:

  1. Usage tier вҖ” "Top 20", "Rising", "Niche picks", "Unused" (most tools show
  you what's popular, but surfacing what's rising or underused is where
  discovery happens)
  2. Role/archetype вҖ” "Fake Out lead", "Speed control", "Trick Room setter",
  "Trick Room attacker", "Weather setter", "Redirect", "Spread damage" (these
  are how VGC players actually think about team composition вҖ” not by type or
  stats)
  3. Your team needs вҖ” This is the big one. Filters that are aware of what your
  current 5 Pokemon are missing:
    - "Covers your Ground weakness"
    - "Adds speed control (your team has none)"
    - "Provides Intimidate (your team has none)"
    - "Adds Fake Out pressure"
  4. Common partners вҖ” "Pairs well with your existing Pokemon" based on meta
  teammate data
  5. Stat thresholds вҖ” "Outspeeds Landorus-T", "Survives Flutter Mane
  Moonblast", functional benchmarks rather than raw numbers
  6. Move access вҖ” "Learns Tailwind", "Learns Follow Me", "Has priority moves"

  What stands out to you from that list? And are there filter types I'm missing
  that you'd want?

вң» Baked for 6m 7s

вқҜ  also given the nature, i also want the builder to show where the bumps are   
  for positive natures                                                          
   В i mean on the sliders when selecting EVs, when the attribute being modified 
   is        в”Ӯ mockup, scratches head*        в”Ӯ    (___)                        
    positively boosted given the nature there are certain points in the EV      
  slider that    в”Ӯ                                в”Ӯв”Җ   .----.                   
    grant 1 extra stat point                                                    

вҸә That's a great detail. For anyone not familiar: at level 50, EV investment
  gives stat points at every 8 EVs (4 EVs = 1 stat point at level 100, but at
  level 50 it's every 8). But with a positive nature (+10% boost), the rounding
  changes вҖ” there are specific EV breakpoints where the nature boost gives you
  an extra point that you wouldn't get without it.

  For example, with a +nature:
  - 4 EVs might give you the same stat as 0 EVs (no bonus)
  - 12 EVs might give +1 over what 8 EVs gives (a "bump")
  - These breakpoints aren't evenly spaced

  So on the EV slider, we'd show tick marks or notches at the EV values where 
  the positive nature grants an extra stat point. This helps users:
  - Know exactly where to invest EVs for maximum efficiency
  - Avoid "wasting" EVs at values between bumps
  - See at a glance that 76 EVs and 80 EVs give the same stat, so put those 4
  EVs elsewhere

  Visually, I'm thinking small tick marks above the slider bar at each bump
  point, maybe in the nature's boost color (green for +nature). The ticks would
  only appear on the stat that has the positive nature boost.

  This also pairs well with the "Max Bulk" preset button вҖ” it could
  auto-distribute EVs to hit exact bump points rather than wastefully dumping
  252 in one stat.

  I'll include this in the spec. Any other details you want to add before I
  write it up?

вқҜ can we see this in the builder

вҸә Let me audit the current species picker mockup against design principles.

  Searched for 1 pattern, read 4 files (ctrl+o to expand)

вҸә Now I have enough theory. Let me audit the screenshot against these
  principles.

  Design Audit: Species Picker

  #: 1
  Severity: Critical
  Problem: No dominant element вҖ” the table and detail panel compete equally for
    attention. Eye has no clear entry point.
  Principle Violated: Ch 6: Dominance вҖ” every composition needs a visual anchor
    the eye is drawn to first
  Fix: Make the detail preview panel the dominant element (larger type, more
    white space). The table is reference data; the preview is where decisions
    happen.
  в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ
  #: 2
  Severity: Critical
  Problem: Tufte 1+1=3 in the table вҖ” every row has a border AND white space
    separation. The table feels heavy and cluttered.
  Principle Violated: Ch 7: Ornamentation вҖ” rule lines between already-spaced
    items create 3 visual separators where 1 suffices
  Fix: Remove row borders entirely. Use alternating subtle background tints and
    generous row padding instead.
  в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ
  #: 3
  Severity: Critical
  Problem: Flat hierarchy in the table вҖ” species name, types, abilities, and
    stats all render at similar visual weight. Everything looks equally
    important.
  Principle Violated: Ch 7: Visual hierarchy вҖ” different pieces of information
    need different visual weight
  Fix: Species name should be clearly dominant in each row. Abilities and types
    should be secondary. Stats should be tertiary (lighter).
  в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ
  #: 4
  Severity: Major
  Problem: Cramped spacing throughout вҖ” elements are packed tight with minimal
    breathing room. The filters bar, table rows, and detail panel all feel
    compressed.
  Principle Violated: Ch 7: White space вҖ” the most powerful and subtle hierarchy

    signal; "the big secret"
  Fix: Increase padding on everything: filters bar, table rows, detail panel
    sections. Use proportional spacing (more space between unrelated groups,
  less
     between related).
  в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ
  #: 5
  Severity: Major
  Problem: No foreground/background depth вҖ” table and detail panel sit on the
    same visual plane. No sense of layering.
  Principle Violated: Ch 6: Foreground/background вҖ” depth cues create layers and

    indicate what's interactive
  Fix: Give the detail preview a slightly elevated background or subtle border
    treatment. The selected row in the table should visually connect to the
    preview.
  в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ
  #: 6
  Severity: Major
  Problem: Type pills are too small and dense вҖ” the colored type badges compete
    with the stat numbers for attention, creating visual noise.
  Principle Violated: Ch 7: Isolated factor layering вҖ” too many visual factors
    changing at once (color + size + shape + text)
  Fix: Make type pills slightly larger with more horizontal padding. Consider
    showing them only in the detail preview, using just text in the table.
  в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ
  #: 7
  Severity: Major
  Problem: Stat columns lack visual hierarchy вҖ” all 6 stat numbers render
    identically. High stats and low stats look the same unless you read each
    number.
  Principle Violated: Ch 6: Contrast вҖ” differences should direct attention
    intentionally
  Fix: Color-code more aggressively: high stats (120+) bold green, mid stats
    neutral, low stats (<70) dimmed. Consider mini inline bars instead of just
    numbers.
  в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ
  #: 8
  Severity: Major
  Problem: VGC Pastes section is too cramped вҖ” three sets stacked with minimal
    spacing, each containing multiple lines of text. Feels like a wall of text.
  Principle Violated: Ch 7: White space + grouping вҖ” related items need
    proximity, unrelated items need separation
  Fix: Give each VGC Paste set more vertical padding. Add a clear divider or
  more
    space between sets. Consider showing only 2 by default with "Show more".
  в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ
  #: 9
  Severity: Minor
  Problem: Filter chips lack grouping вҖ” usage tier, category filters, and
    team-need filters all run together in one line with only pipe separators.
  Principle Violated: Ch 7: Grouping вҖ” conceptually related items should be
    visually grouped
  Fix: Group filter categories with slightly more space or subtle background
    tints. The pipe separators are too subtle.
  в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ
  #: 10
  Severity: Minor
  Problem: No rhythm in the detail panel вҖ” sections (stats, info, team fit, VGC
    pastes) have inconsistent spacing and no repeating visual pattern.
  Principle Violated: Ch 6: Rhythm вҖ” repeating patterns create scannability
  Fix: Use consistent section spacing and a repeating section header style.

  Summary: The core issues are density (too much info, not enough space), flat
  hierarchy (everything at the same visual weight), and lack of a dominant focal
   point. The data is all there вҖ” it just needs to breathe and have a clear
  visual priority order.

  Recommended next steps:
  1. /color to establish better contrast between primary/secondary/tertiary
  information
  2. /fonts to set up a proper type scale with meaningful size differences
  3. /flow for hover states and the tableвҶ’detail connection interaction

  Want me to apply these fixes to the mockup now?

  I see your two messages. Let me address both:

  Discover and Meta as tabs: You're right вҖ” Discover makes more sense as part of
   the species picker (it's about finding Pokemon/sets), and Meta feels like it
  should be accessible separately from the per-Pokemon editor. Here are some
  options for Meta:

  - A) Collapsible sidebar that slides in from the right edge вҖ” an overlay panel
   you can toggle on/off without replacing the context tabs. Like a "meta
  drawer."
  - B) Format-level page вҖ” Meta lives at /dashboard/teams/[id]/meta as a sibling
   route, not inside the editor. You navigate to it from the team header.
  - C) Inline in the editor вҖ” When you hover/click on a field (ability, item,
  move), the Meta data for that specific field appears as a tooltip/popover.
  "38% of Lando-T run AV" shows when you're editing the item field.

  Option C is interesting because it puts meta data exactly where you need it вҖ”
  at the moment of decision. Instead of a dedicated Meta tab, the meta insights
  are woven into the editing experience.

  Descriptions for abilities, items, moves: Completely agree вҖ” when you hover or
   click on a move like "Ice Spinner", you should see BP, accuracy, type,
  category (physical/special), secondary effects, and a description. Same for
  abilities and items. This could be tooltips on hover, or expand inline when
  editing.

  What's your instinct on where Meta should live?

  Option A: Meta Drawer

вң» Churned for 2m 57s

вқҜ i think the answer is a combination                                           

вҸә That makes sense. Here's how the three layers work together:

  Option B (Meta Page) вҖ” for when you want to study the format. "What's the meta
   look like? What archetypes am I facing? How does my team fit?" This is a
  deliberate, research-mode activity. Sub-nav: Builder | Meta.

  Option A (Meta Drawer) вҖ” for quick reference while editing. "What's the most
  popular item on this Lando-T?" Toggle it open, glance at the data, close it.
  Per-Pokemon, ambient.

  Option C (Inline Tooltips) вҖ” for in-the-moment decisions. When you're choosing
   an item and the picker shows "Safety Goggles 34% / Sitrus 22% / AV 18%" right
   in the dropdown вҖ” that's meta data woven into the editing flow. No extra
  click needed.

  Three levels of depth for the same data:
  - Editing a field вҶ’ C gives you the number inline
  - Want more context вҶ’ A gives you the full breakdown without leaving the
  editor
  - Want the full picture вҶ’ B gives you the format-level analysis

  That also settles the tab situation. The right panel tabs become just Types, 
  Speed, Calc вҖ” three focused analysis tools. Meta and Discover are handled
  elsewhere (Meta via drawer + page + inline, Discover via the species picker).

  Want me to write the spec now? I think we've covered enough ground to document
   everything.

  technical requirements to make this all work.

   out. Let me explore what already exists and identify the gaps.

вҸә Excellent findings. Here's the technical picture:

  What we already have (reusable):
  - Full stat calculator (level 50, nature boosts, EVs/IVs)
  - Type effectiveness + team coverage + synergy analysis
  - Showdown format parser (bidirectional)
  - Format validation via @pkmn/sim

  - All @pkmn packages (dex, data, sim, sets, img)

  Key technical questions I want to surface:

  1. Damage calculator вҖ” should we use @smogon/calc (the same engine Showdown
  uses) or build our own? Using @smogon/calc gives us accuracy for free but adds
   a dependency.
  2. Meta data source вҖ” you mentioned Limitless API key. For V1, should we seed
  from Limitless only, or also aggregate from our own tournament_team_sheets
  data?
  3. Client vs server for calculations вҖ” stat calcs, type coverage, damage
  calcs, speed tiers вҖ” these should all run client-side for instant feedback,
  right? The @pkmn/dex data is already loaded client-side.
  4. Team auto-save вҖ” should edits save immediately (optimistic UI) or require
  explicit save? Optimistic feels better for a builder.

  What are your thoughts on these? Then I'll write up the full technical spec.

вҸә Fetch(https://github.com/smogon/damage-calc)

вҸә Good research. Here's what I'm thinking:

  Supabase Analytics Buckets вҖ” interesting but probably not the right tool for
  V1. They're designed for huge datasets (data warehouse scale) and are still in
   early development with breaking changes. Our meta data is relatively small вҖ”
  even tracking every Pokemon's usage across every format is maybe tens of
  thousands of rows, not millions. Regular Postgres tables with proper indexes
  will handle this fine. We can always migrate to Analytics Buckets later if the
   data volume grows. For now, keeping it in the main database means simpler
  queries and no additional infrastructure.

  @smogon/calc вҖ” this is the clear choice for the damage calculator. It's the
  same engine Pokemonshowdown.com uses, supports Gen 1-9, actively maintained,
  and gives us accurate damage ranges for free. No reason to reimplement the
  damage formula ourselves.

  On your point about integrating with existing tools вҖ” here's my thinking on
  what to leverage vs build:

  в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ

вң» Cogitated for 32s

вқҜ that makes sense i agree with not using supabase analytics buckets in the     
  short term. how are we going to track meta changes over time? i think a big   
  part of this is showing the historical changes overtime                       

вҸә Great question вҖ” this is one of the core differentiators. Pikalytics shows you
   today's usage. We want to show you "Chien-Pao was 22% three weeks ago, now
  it's 28.5% and climbing вҖ” here's why."

  There are a few approaches:

  Approach 1: Append-only snapshots (simplest)
  Every time we import data (say daily), we append new rows with a timestamp. No
   updates, no deletes вҖ” just keep adding.

  pokemon_format_stats:
    id, snapshot_date, format, species, usage_pct, rank, ...

  -- "Chien-Pao usage in Reg I over time"
  SELECT snapshot_date, usage_pct
  FROM pokemon_format_stats
  WHERE format = 'reg-i' AND species = 'Chien-Pao'
  ORDER BY snapshot_date

  Simple to implement, simple to query. The table grows by (num_pokemon Г—
  num_formats) rows per snapshot. At ~200 Pokemon Г— 5 formats Г— daily = ~1000
  rows/day = ~365K rows/year. That's nothing for Postgres.

  Approach 2: Current + history (optimized reads)
  Two tables: pokemon_format_stats_current (always the latest, fast reads for
  the UI) and pokemon_format_stats_history (append-only, for trend queries).
  Import replaces current, appends to history.

  More complex but faster reads for the common case (showing current meta).

  Approach 3: Postgres partitioning by month
  Same as Approach 1 but with monthly table partitions. Postgres handles this
  natively. Old months get compressed/archived automatically. Queries across
  time ranges are efficient.

  ---
  My recommendation: Approach 1 with a few additions. Here's the schema I'm
  thinking:

  -- When was data imported and from where?
  meta_snapshots:
    id, source (limitless | internal | manual),
    format, snapshot_date, created_at

  -- Per-species stats at each snapshot
  pokemon_format_stats:
    id, snapshot_id FK, format, species,
    usage_pct, rank,
    usage_change_7d, usage_change_30d,  -- precomputed deltas
    sample_size,
    created_at

  -- Per-species detailed breakdowns
  pokemon_moveset_stats:
    id, snapshot_id FK, format, species,
    -- Items
    item, item_usage_pct,
    -- Abilities
    ability, ability_usage_pct,
    -- Moves (denormalized for query speed)
    move, move_usage_pct,
    -- Spreads
    nature, ev_spread, spread_usage_pct,
    -- Teammates
    teammate_species, teammate_pct,
    -- Tera types
    tera_type, tera_usage_pct

  The usage_change_7d and usage_change_30d columns get precomputed during import
   вҖ” that way the UI can show "вҶ— +3.2%" without running a window query every
  time.

  For import cadence: daily makes sense. Run a cron edge function that:
  1. Fetches from Limitless API
  2. Computes deltas against the previous snapshot
  3. Inserts new snapshot + stats rows
  4. Busts the cache tags

  The historical data also feeds the "Rising" and "Falling" filters in the
  species picker вҖ” those are just WHERE usage_change_7d > threshold.

  One more thing: we should also aggregate our own tournament data over time. As
   trainers.gg hosts more tournaments, the tournament_team_sheets table becomes
  a valuable data source for meta trends specific to our community. We could run
   a separate aggregation that computes usage stats from our own tournaments and
   merges it with Limitless data.

  Does this schema direction feel right? And what's the import cadence you'd
  want вҖ” daily? More frequent?

вң» Brewed for 36s

вқҜ i havn't read your previous response yet so giving more information, data is  
  going to be constantly be updated so we need to take that into account. so    
  there is data generated from running tournaments natively on the site. that   
  is 1 part. another part is the tournament data being imported from Limitless. 
   those are sent over via a webhook but only when a tournament finishes. then  
  there is data from rk9 which houses the official tournament data for          
  regionals, international champion ships, worlds, and special events. we don't 
   have the webhook built for limtiless yet nor do we have the integration      
  built to scrape rk9 (doesnt have an api)                                      

вҸә This is important context that changes the architecture. Let me revise my
  thinking.

  The data isn't "pull from one API daily" вҖ” it's event-driven from three 
  sources arriving at different times:

  Source: Native tournaments
  Trigger: Real-time as tournaments run on trainers.gg
  Status: Built (tournament_team_sheets)
  Data Quality: Full sets (EVs, IVs, natures, moves)
  в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ
  Source: Limitless
  Trigger: Webhook when tournament finishes
  Status: Not built yet
  Data Quality: Likely OTS-level (species, moves, item, ability, tera)
  в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ
  Source: RK9
  Trigger: Scraping (no API)
  Status: Not built yet
  Data Quality: OTS-level from official events

  This means the meta picture is continuously being updated as new tournament
  results flow in from any source. Not a daily snapshot вҖ” an evolving aggregate.

  Here's the architecture I'd propose:

  Layer 1: Raw tournament results (source of truth)
  tournament_results:
    id, source (native | limitless | rk9),
    external_id,          -- Limitless tournament ID, RK9 event ID
    tournament_name,
    format,
    date,
    player_count,
    imported_at

  tournament_result_teams:
    id, tournament_result_id FK,
    player_name,
    placement,            -- 1st, top 4, top 8, top 16, etc.
    species,              -- one row per Pokemon per team
    position (1-6),
    ability, held_item, tera_type,
    move1, move2, move3, move4,
    -- Full data only available from native tournaments:
    nature, ev_spread, iv_spread  (nullable)

  Every tournament from every source gets normalized into these tables. This is
  append-only вҖ” we never update, just add.

  Layer 2: Aggregated meta stats (computed)
  format_meta_stats:
    id, format,
    computed_at,           -- when this aggregate was last recomputed
    period_start,          -- e.g. "last 30 days" window start
    period_end,
    total_teams,           -- how many teams in this window
    total_tournaments

  pokemon_usage_stats:
    id, format_meta_id FK,
    species, usage_pct, rank,
    usage_change_7d, usage_change_30d,
    sample_size

  pokemon_detail_stats:
    id, format_meta_id FK,
    species,
    -- Each of these is a JSONB array of {value, pct} pairs
    items jsonb,           -- [{item: "Clear Amulet", pct: 32}, ...]
    abilities jsonb,       -- [{ability: "Sword of Ruin", pct: 98}, ...]
    moves jsonb,           -- [{move: "Ice Spinner", pct: 88}, ...]
    spreads jsonb,         -- [{nature: "Adamant", evs: "252/4/0/0/0/252", pct:
  42}, ...]
    tera_types jsonb,      -- [{type: "Poison", pct: 28}, ...]
    teammates jsonb        -- [{species: "Urshifu", pct: 58}, ...]

  Layer 3: Recomputation trigger

  When new data arrives (native tournament ends, Limitless webhook fires, RK9
  scrape completes):
  1. Raw data gets inserted into Layer 1
  2. A database function or edge function recomputes Layer 2 for the affected
  format
  3. Uses a sliding window вҖ” "last 30 days" or "last N tournaments" вҖ” so the
  meta always reflects recent trends
  4. The old aggregate row stays (for historical comparison), new one gets
  created
  5. Cache tags get busted so the UI picks up fresh data

  The key insight: Layer 2 is recomputed, not appended. Each recomputation
  creates a new format_meta_stats row with a computed_at timestamp. The UI
  always reads the latest one. But we keep the old ones so we can show "what the
   meta looked like 2 weeks ago" and compute trend lines.

  For historical trends:
  Since we keep every format_meta_stats recomputation, we can query across time:
  -- Chien-Pao usage trend in Reg I over the last 3 months
  SELECT computed_at, usage_pct
  FROM pokemon_usage_stats pus
  JOIN format_meta_stats fms ON pus.format_meta_id = fms.id
  WHERE fms.format = 'reg-i' AND pus.species = 'Chien-Pao'
  ORDER BY fms.computed_at

  Sliding window vs all-time:
  The meta stats should probably use a sliding window (last 30 days or last 20
  tournaments) rather than all-time, since the meta shifts. But we could offer
  both views вҖ” "current meta" (30-day window) vs "full season" (all data since
  format started).

  JSONB for detail stats:
  Using JSONB for items/moves/spreads/teammates means we store one row per
  species per snapshot instead of hundreds of rows. Simpler to query, faster to
  read, and the data is always read as a complete set anyway.

  The three data pipelines that need building (in priority order):
  1. Native вҖ” already have the data in tournament_team_sheets, just need the
  aggregation
  2. Limitless webhook вҖ” needs webhook endpoint + data normalization
  3. RK9 scraper вҖ” needs scraping infrastructure, probably runs on a schedule
  after major events

  Does this architecture make sense? Any of these data source assumptions off?

вҸә This is shaping up to be a serious data pipeline. Let me map out all four
  sources with their constraints:

  Source: Native (trainers.gg)
  Trigger: Real-time during tournament
  Granularity: Full sets + match results + replays
  Data Available: EVs, IVs, natures, moves, items, abilities, tera, W/L per
    round, lead pairs
  в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ
  Source: Limitless webhook
  Trigger: On tournament completion
  Granularity: Tournament-level batch
  Data Available: Team sheets (OTS level), placements, player count
  в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ
  Source: RK9 scraping
  Trigger: Post-event scrape
  Granularity: Tournament-level batch
  Data Available: Team sheets from official events, placements
  в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ
  Source: Showdown replays
  Trigger: Parsed from public replays
  Granularity: Per-game granularity
  Data Available: Moves used, leads, switches, damage dealt, KOs, win/loss вҖ”
    actual battle data

  The Showdown replay parsing is a big addition. That's a completely different
  kind of data вҖ” it's not "what did people bring" but "what did people actually
  do in battle." That feeds:
  - Actual move usage (not just "has the move" but "used it in X% of games")
  - Lead pair data (what gets brought to the front most often)
  - Win rates by Pokemon (which Pokemon contribute most to wins)
  - Bring rates (out of 6, which 4 get brought most)
  - KO stats (what's KOing what in practice)

  That's the kind of data that makes the smart damage calc suggestions really
  good вҖ” instead of just "meta Lando-T uses Earthquake," you can say "Lando-T
  used Earthquake into Chien-Pao in 43% of games where they faced each other,
  KOing 78% of the time."

  Here's my revised thinking on the architecture with all four sources:

  Layer 1: Raw data (per-source, append-only)

  -- Source tracking
  data_imports:
    id, source (native | limitless | rk9 | showdown),
    external_ref,        -- Limitless ID, RK9 event ID, replay URL
    format,
    imported_at

  -- Tournament-level data (from native, limitless, rk9)
  imported_tournament_results:
    id, import_id FK,
    tournament_name, format, date,
    player_count, source

  imported_team_sheets:
    id, tournament_result_id FK,
    player_name, placement,
    position (1-6),
    species, ability, held_item, tera_type,
    move1-4,
    -- Only from native tournaments:
    nature, ev_spread, iv_spread (nullable)

  -- Battle-level data (from Showdown replays)
  imported_replays:
    id, import_id FK,
    replay_url, format, upload_date,
    player1, player2, winner,
    turns

  imported_replay_actions:
    id, replay_id FK,
    turn, player,
    pokemon_species,
    action_type (move | switch | tera),
    move_used, target,
    damage_pct (nullable),
    ko (boolean)

  Layer 2: Aggregated stats (computed from Layer 1)

  Same as before but now enriched with battle data:
  pokemon_usage_stats:
    -- from team sheets:
    usage_pct, rank, usage_change_7d/30d
    -- from replays:
    bring_rate,          -- % of games where brought (out of 6вҶ’4)
    win_rate,            -- % of games won when brought
    avg_kos_per_game

  pokemon_detail_stats:
    items, abilities, moves, spreads,
    tera_types, teammates (jsonb arrays)
    -- from replays:
    actual_move_usage jsonb,    -- moves actually clicked, not just carried
    common_leads jsonb,         -- lead pair frequency
    common_targets jsonb        -- "Earthquake used into X species Y% of the
  time"

  For native trainers.gg tournaments вҖ” the tight integration you mentioned.
  Since we control the data, we can capture everything:
  - Full team sets (EVs/IVs/natures) вҖ” already in tournament_team_sheets
  - Match results per round вҖ” already in the tournament system
  - Which 4 were brought each game (if we add a "brought" field to match
  reporting)
  - Lead pairs (if captured during match reporting)

  This means native tournaments are the highest-fidelity data source. The meta
  stats can weight native data more heavily or show it separately ("trainers.gg
  community meta" vs "global meta").

  Showdown replay parsing вҖ” this is probably the most technically complex piece.
   We'd need:
  1. A list of replay URLs to parse (from Showdown's public replay search API)
  2. A parser that reads the battle log format (it's a text protocol)
  3. Extract actions, KOs, switches, tera usage per turn
  4. Store normalized into imported_replays/imported_replay_actions
  5. Run periodically (cron edge function that fetches recent replays for
  tracked formats)

  There's an existing library @pkmn/protocol that can parse Showdown's battle
  protocol. Worth checking if it's already in our dependencies or if we need to
  add it.

  Does this feel like the right direction? And for scope вҖ” which of these four
  sources should be in V1 vs later?

  My instinct: V1 = native data aggregation + basic Showdown parsing. Limitless
  webhook and RK9 scraping can come in V2 since they need external integrations
  to build.

вқҜ one fundamental thing you have wrong is that  native data, evs, ivs, nature   
  are not shared by default. only the open teamsheet format is shared when

вҸә Important correction. Let me fix my understanding:

  Open Team Sheet (OTS) = what's shared publicly by default:
  - Species, ability, held item, tera type, moves (4 moves)
  - That's it. No EVs, no IVs, no nature, no nicknames.

  Full team data = private unless the user opts in:
  - EVs, IVs, nature, level вҖ” stored in the pokemon table via team_pokemon вҶ’
  teams
  - Only visible if the user explicitly makes the team public (is_public = true)

  So for meta data aggregation from native tournaments, the baseline data
  available is OTS-level вҖ” same granularity as Limitless and RK9. We can report:
  - Species usage %
  - Item usage per species
  - Ability usage per species
  - Move usage per species
  - Tera type usage per species

  We cannot report EV spreads or natures from native tournaments unless users
  opt in to sharing their full team. That's a big difference вҖ” it means
  spread/nature data can only come from:

  1. Showdown replays вҖ” if we can reverse-engineer spreads from damage calcs in
  the replay (hard, unreliable)
  2. Users who make teams public вҖ” opt-in, likely a small subset
  3. VGC Pastes / content creators вҖ” who voluntarily share full sets
  4. Showdown usage stats вҖ” Smogon publishes monthly usage dumps that include
  common spreads

  This means the "common spreads" section in the Meta view has a different data
  source than the "usage %" section. Usage comes from tournament OTS data (high
  volume, reliable). Spreads come from voluntary sharing + Showdown stats (lower
   volume, less direct).

  That also affects the species picker вҖ” when we show "popular sets from VGC
  Pastes," those are voluntarily shared full sets. But when we show "42.1% usage
   in Reg I," that comes from OTS data across tournaments.

  The smart damage calc suggestions would use Showdown usage data for common
  spreads (e.g., "most Lando-T run 252 HP / 252 Atk Adamant") rather than our
  own tournament data, since we won't have spread data from most players.

  Does that match your understanding? And is there a mechanism in the tournament
   flow where users could opt in to sharing their full team data вҖ” like a toggle
   when submitting a team sheet?

вқҜ in the short term, we do not have the play by play data for matches for       
  tournaments ran on the site. but i am brainstorming a feature that would let  
  us add that.                                                                  

вҸә That's a great long-term play. If you eventually add play-by-play match
  reporting for native tournaments (even simplified вҖ” like "select your leads,
  report KOs, report winner"), that would give trainers.gg the highest-fidelity
  competitive data of any platform. Nobody else has structured game-level data
  from real tournaments.

  But for now, let me work with what's realistic for V1.

  V1 data sources:
  - Native tournaments вҶ’ OTS-level data (species, ability, item, tera, moves) +
  placement + W/L record
  - Showdown replays вҶ’ parsed battle data (actual moves used, leads, KOs, win

  - Limitless webhook вҶ’ OTS-level data when tournament completes (needs

  - RK9 scraping вҶ’ OTS-level data from official events (needs building, lower

  V1 meta data we can actually show:

  в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
  в”Ӯ        Data Point        в”Ӯ             Source              в”Ӯ Confidence в”Ӯ
  в”ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Ө

  в”Ӯ Actual move-in-battle    в”Ӯ Showdown replays                в”Ӯ Medium     в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ usage                    в”Ӯ                                 в”Ӯ            в”Ӯ

  в”Ӯ Lead pairs + bring rates в”Ӯ Showdown replays                в”Ӯ Medium     в”Ӯ
  в”ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Ө
  в”Ӯ Win rates per Pokemon    в”Ӯ Native W/L + Showdown replays   в”Ӯ Medium     в”Ӯ
  в”ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Ө
  в”Ӯ Placement correlation    в”Ӯ OTS + placement from all        в”Ӯ High       в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ                          в”Ӯ sources                         в”Ӯ            в”Ӯ
  в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

  I think we have enough of the technical picture now to write the spec. Let me
  summarize what we've landed on across this entire brainstorm, and write it up.
   There's one last thing I want to confirm before I do:

  For the V1 spec scope, here's what I'm including:

  In scope:
  - Team builder workspace (split panel, horizontal strip, editor, context tabs)
  - Species picker (inline, full-width, Showdown-style table + detail panel,
  smart filters, VGC Pastes sets)
  - Context panel: Types, Speed, Calc (3 tabs)
  - Meta: drawer (A) + page (B) + inline tooltips (C) вҖ” all three layers
  - EV editor with nature bumps
  - Move/item/ability descriptions and meta usage % in pickers
  - Import (Showdown paste, Pokepaste URL)
  - Export (Showdown format)
  - Team CRUD (create, edit, delete, fork)
  - Format validation
  - Data pipeline architecture (raw вҶ’ aggregate, multi-source)
  - Database schema for meta stats

  Deferred to later:
  - Matchups/SPAMS
  - Matches/PASRS/vsrecorder
  - Team versioning/branching
  - Collaborative editing (websockets)
  - Private sharing with revocable access
  - Limitless webhook (architecture documented but not built)
  - RK9 scraping
  - Showdown replay parsing
  - Play-by-play match data for native tournaments

  Does that scope feel right?

вқҜ also with this data on the meta one of the things i want to do is add         
  weights. like for example lets say that Urshifu is on 50% of all teams. that  
  is super valuable information to know. but it is also super valuable to know  
  how many teams in topcut have urshifu, is it higher? is it lower? something   
  with data from limitless and rk9                                              

вҸә Excellent point. Raw usage doesn't tell you if a Pokemon is good вҖ” just
  popular. A Pokemon could be on 50% of teams but only 30% of top cut teams,
  meaning it's overplayed. Or it could be on 20% of teams but 45% of top cut,
  meaning it's underrated and overperforming.

  So we need weighted usage tiers:

  в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
  в”Ӯ    Metric     в”Ӯ   What It Tells You    в”Ӯ            Source             в”Ӯ
  в”ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Ө
  в”Ӯ Overall usage в”Ӯ How popular is it?     в”Ӯ All teams across all          в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ  %            в”Ӯ                        в”Ӯ tournaments                   в”Ӯ
  в”ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Ө
  в”Ӯ Top cut usage в”Ӯ How good is it?        в”Ӯ Only teams that made top cut  в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ  %            в”Ӯ                        в”Ӯ                               в”Ӯ
  в”ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Ө
  в”Ӯ Win rate      в”Ӯ How often does it win? в”Ӯ W/L from native + Showdown    в”Ӯ
  в”ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Ө
  в”Ӯ Conversion    в”Ӯ Does it convert to top в”Ӯ top_cut_usage / overall_usage в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ rate          в”Ӯ  cut?                  в”Ӯ  ratio                        в”Ӯ
  в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

  A conversion rate > 1.0 means the Pokemon overperforms (more common in top cut
   than in the field). < 1.0 means it underperforms (popular but doesn't make
  cuts).

  This is exactly the kind of insight that Pikalytics and Munchstats don't show
  вҖ” they mostly report ladder usage without placement weighting. Limitless and
  RK9 data is what makes this possible because they have placement data attached
   to team sheets.

  The data model needs placement tiers on the imported team sheets:

  imported_team_sheets:
    ...existing fields...
    placement_tier enum:
      'champion'     -- 1st place
      'finalist'     -- 2nd place
      'top4'         -- top 4
      'top8'         -- top 8
      'top16'        -- top 16
      'top_cut'      -- made cut but didn't place above
      'day2'         -- made day 2
      'completed'    -- entered, didn't cut

  Then the aggregation computes stats at each tier:

  pokemon_usage_stats:
    ...existing fields...
    usage_pct,              -- all teams
    usage_pct_top_cut,      -- top cut only
    usage_pct_top8,         -- top 8 only
    conversion_rate,        -- top_cut / overall
    avg_placement_score,    -- weighted placement metric

  In the UI, this shows up as:

  - Species picker: "Urshifu вҖ” 50% usage (26% top cut, 0.52 conversion)" вҖ”
  immediately tells you it's popular but underperforming
  - Meta page: Pokemon ranked by different metrics вҖ” toggle between "Most Used"
  / "Best Performing" / "Most Overperforming (rising gems)" / "Most Overplayed
  (falling traps)"
  - Smart suggestions: "Your team has 3 Pokemon with conversion rate > 1.2 вҖ”
  this core overperforms in tournament results"

  The "Rising gems" filter in the species picker becomes really powerful вҖ”
  Pokemon with low overall usage but high top cut rate are exactly what
  competitive players want to find. That's the kind of insight that wins
  tournaments.

  For RK9 data specifically, the placement tiers are even more meaningful
  because regionals/internationals/worlds are the highest-stakes events. We
  could weight those placements more heavily вҖ” a top 8 at worlds means more than
   a top 8 at a 32-person local.

  data_imports:
    ...existing fields...
    event_tier enum:
      'worlds'
      'international'
      'regional'
      'special_event'
      'midseason_showdown'
      'community'          -- Limitless/native
      'online'             -- online tournaments

  The weighting formula could be something like:
  - Worlds placement: 5x weight
  - International: 3x weight
  - Regional: 2x weight
  - Community/online: 1x weight

  So a top 8 Worlds finish with Urshifu counts as much as five community
  tournament top 8s.

  I'm adding this to the spec scope вҖ” weighted meta stats with placement tiers
  and event tier weighting. This is a genuine differentiator.

  Ready to write the spec now?

вқҜ now one thing to keep in mind is that when we import data from limitless and  
  rk9, we are going to need to maintain a completely distinct set of users.     
  since there is no way to know if the owners of 2 accounts with the same       
  username are actually the same person.                                        

вҸә Critical point. We can't merge identities across platforms вҖ” "WolfeyGlick" on
  Limitless, "WolfeyGlick" on RK9, and "wolfey" on trainers.gg could be three
  different people (or the same person, but we can't assume).

  So we need a player identity system that keeps external players separate:

  external_players:
    id,
    source (limitless | rk9 | showdown),
    source_player_id,        -- their ID on that platform
    display_name,            -- their username on that platform
    -- Optional: linked trainers.gg alt
    linked_alt_id FK(alts) nullable,
    linked_at,
    linked_by (self | admin),
    UNIQUE(source, source_player_id)

  Key rules:
  - External players are never auto-linked to trainers.gg accounts
  - Same display name across sources = separate external_players rows
  - Linking is opt-in вҖ” a trainers.gg user can claim "this Limitless account is
  me" (with verification)
  - Until linked, tournament results from external sources show the external
  display name, not a trainers.gg profile

  For the imported team sheets:
  imported_team_sheets:
    ...existing fields...
    external_player_id FK(external_players),
    -- NOT linked to alts directly

  Benefits of this approach:
  - No false identity merges
  - Users can build a unified tournament history by claiming their external
  accounts
  - We can still show "player X got 1st at Portland Regional" without needing
  them to be a trainers.gg user
  - The meta stats aggregation doesn't care about identity вҖ” it just counts
  species/items/moves across all team sheets regardless of who played them

  The claiming flow (future feature):
  1. User goes to their profile settings
  2. "Link external accounts" вҖ” Limitless, RK9, Showdown
  3. For Limitless: maybe OAuth or display name verification
  4. For RK9: probably manual claim + admin verification (since RK9 uses real
  names)
  5. Once linked, their tournament history from that source appears on their
  trainers.gg profile

  For V1, we just store external players as-is with no linking. The
  linking/claiming is a future feature.

  This also matters for the Discover tab / VGC Pastes вҖ” when we show "by
  @WolfeyGlick, 1st Portland Regional," that's an external_players display name,
   not a trainers.gg user. If they later join trainers.gg and link their
  account, the attribution updates.

  Good catch вҖ” I'll include this in the spec. Anything else before I write it
  up?
вқҜ correct i d plan to add a linking feature in the future for now that is not   
  important

вҸә You're right вҖ” there are several open threads. Let me surface them:

  UI decisions we never finalized:

  1. Move/item/ability descriptions вҖ” We agreed to show BP, accuracy, secondary
  effects, ability descriptions, item effects. But how? Tooltip on hover? Expand
   inline when the field is focused? A persistent info bar?
  2. The normal editor view вҖ” We redesigned the picker to use horizontal strip +
   full width, but never went back and mocked the normal editing state with the
  horizontal strip. The split panel (editor left, context tabs right) needs
  updating to match.
  3. Inline meta tooltips (Option C) вҖ” We agreed these should exist, but what
  exactly triggers them? When you open the item picker and see "Safety Goggles
  34%", is the 34% clickable to see more? Or is there a more passive way to
  surface it?
  4. Validation feedback вҖ” When a team has legality issues (duplicate items,
  illegal moves, EV overflow), how does that surface? Red badges on the strip? A
   validation panel? Inline errors on the fields?
  5. Empty states вҖ” What does the workspace look like with 0 Pokemon? With 1?
  What does the right panel show when there's nothing to analyze?

  Technical decisions unanswered:

  6. Auto-save vs explicit save вҖ” I asked this earlier and it never got
  answered. Should edits save immediately (optimistic UI, no save button) or
  require the user to click "Save"?
  7. State management вҖ” The editor has a lot of local state (currently editing
  Pokemon, unsaved changes, picker open/closed). TanStack Query for server
  state, but what manages the editor form state?
  8. URL structure вҖ” Is it /dashboard/teams/[id] for the builder and
  /dashboard/teams/[id]/meta for the meta page? Or query params?

  Data/scope questions:

  9. Builder without meta data вҖ” Should the team builder work as a standalone
  editor even before any meta pipeline is built? That would let us ship the
  builder first and layer meta data on later.
  10. VGC Pastes data source вҖ” We keep referencing "proven sets from VGC Pastes"
   but never identified how we actually get that data. Is it scraped? Manual
  entry? An API?
  11. Showdown usage dumps вҖ” These are the source for common spreads/natures. Do
   you know where these are published and how often?

  Which of these do you want to tackle?

вҸә That's a format-level difference. So the builder needs to be format-aware for

  - VGC (Scarlet/Violet): EVs + IVs both exist. IVs matter (0 Atk, custom Speed

  - Pokemon Champions: No IVs вҖ” only "effort values" equivalent. Hide IV

вҸә Crystal clear вҖ” format-awareness is a core requirement, not a nice-to-have.
  The builder adapts its entire editor UI based on the selected format:

  - Which fields exist (IVs yes/no, natures, tera types, etc.)
  - Which Pokemon/moves/abilities/items are legal
  - Validation rules
  - The format registry in packages/pokemon/src/formats.ts drives all of this

  And for VGC formats with IVs вҖ” always show both EVs and IVs, no hiding.

  - Descriptions inline in pickers (like Showdown), hover tooltips on selected

  - Validation: strip badges + inline field errors + validation summary panel

  - 3 context tabs: Types, Speed, Calc

   V1)
  - Format-aware editor from day one
  - IVs + EVs always visible (for formats that have both)
  - External players stored separately, no auto-linking

  вҺҝ В Plan saved to: ~/.claude/plans/spicy-drifting-bird.md В· /plan to edit
     Pokemon Team Builder вҖ” Design & Technical Spec

     Context

     trainers.gg needs a full-featured Pokemon team builder that integrates into
      the existing dashboard. Currently, teams can only be created by pasting
     Showdown text during tournament registration. This spec defines a
     standalone team builder that serves as a competitive Pokemon workbench вҖ”
     editing, analysis, and meta intelligence in one place. The builder ships
     first as a standalone editor with analysis tools (Types, Speed, Calc). Meta
      data integration, matchup planning (SPAMS), and match tracking (PASRS)
     layer on later when their respective data pipelines are ready.

     What prompted this: The competitive landscape shows 10+ fragmented tools
     (Showdown builder, Pikalytics, Marriland, SPAMS spreadsheet, vsrecorder,
     etc.) that players juggle. trainers.gg unifies these into a single
     integrated experience. The team builder is the central hub.

     Intended outcome: A production-ready team builder that competitive Pokemon
     players prefer over Showdown's built-in builder, with clear extension
     points for meta analytics, matchup planning, and match tracking.

     ---
     V1 Scope

     In Scope

     - Team builder workspace (split panel, horizontal team strip, editor, 3
     context tabs)
     - Inline species picker (full-width, Showdown-style table + detail panel,
     smart filters, VGC Pastes sets)
     - Context panel: Types, Speed, Calc (3 tabs)
     - Format-aware editor from day one (VGC, Smogon, Champions)
     - EV editor with nature bump indicators
     - IV editor (always visible for formats that support IVs, hidden for
     Champions)
     - Move/item/ability pickers with inline descriptions (BP, accuracy,
     effects, usage %)
     - Nickname, gender (when relevant), shiny toggle, level
     - Import: Showdown paste (full team + per-Pokemon), Pokepaste URL
     - Export: Showdown paste (clipboard), Pokepaste link, trainers.gg shareable
      link вҖ” full team + per-Pokemon
     - Team CRUD: create, edit, delete, fork (with parent link, choose alt)
     - Drag-and-drop reordering in the team strip
     - Format validation: strip badges + inline field errors + validation
     summary panel
     - Auto-save with debounce (2s inactivity)
     - Team notes + per-Pokemon notes
     - Empty state: workspace visible with add/import prompts
     - Teams list page with format filters (default: active format), grouping by
      format
     - Data pipeline architecture (schema designed, not fully implemented in V1)
     - Database schema for meta stats + external players

     Deferred (architecture documented, not built)

     - Meta data integration (drawer + inline tooltips вҖ” placement TBD)
     - Meta data pipeline (Limitless webhook, RK9 scraping, Showdown replay
     parsing)
     - VGC Pastes data import
     - Matchup planning (SPAMS)
     - Match tracking (PASRS/vsrecorder)
     - Team versioning/branching UI (fork with parent_team_id is V1, branching
     UI is later)
     - Collaborative editing (websockets)
     - Private sharing with revocable access
     - Play-by-play match data for native tournaments
     - External player account linking

     ---
     UI Design

     Overall Layout

     The builder lives in the dashboard at /dashboard/alts/[handle]/teams.

     Teams list page (/dashboard/alts/[handle]/teams):
     - Default filter: current active format (e.g., Reg I)
     - Format filter chips: All, Reg I, Reg H, Smogon OU, etc.
     - When "All" selected, teams grouped by format with section headers
     - Team cards show: 6 Pokemon sprites, team name, format, last updated,
     version info, W/L record (when available)
     - Actions: "+ New Team", "Import Paste"

     New team dialog:
     - Name, format selector, start from (empty / import paste / fork existing)
     - Creating opens the workspace

     Team workspace (/dashboard/alts/[handle]/teams/[id]):
     - Dashboard sidebar collapsed to icons on the left
     - Horizontal team strip centered at top (6 Pokemon chips + empty slots)
     - Below the strip: split panel вҖ” editor (50%) left, context tabs (50%)
     right
     - Header bar: breadcrumb (вҶҗ Teams / Team Name), format badge, action
     buttons (Import, Export, Fork, Share, Validate)

     Team Strip (horizontal, centered)

     - Each chip shows: sprite, species name, held item
     - Selected chip: teal highlight + border
     - Empty slots: dashed border, "+" icon
     - Drag-and-drop to reorder positions
     - Click chip to select that Pokemon for editing
     - Click "+" to open species picker

     Editor Panel (left 50%)

     - Species header: clickable species name with в–ҫ indicator (opens species
     picker), type pills, level
     - Fields (2-column grid, click-to-edit):
       - Ability (picker with description + usage %)
       - Held Item (picker with description + duplicate item warning)
       - Nature (picker showing +/- stat effects)
       - Tera Type (type selector вҖ” format-dependent, Champions may differ)
       - Nickname (optional text field)
       - Gender (selector, shown only when relevant for the species)
       - Shiny (toggle icon)
     - Moves (2-column grid, 4 slots):
       - Click slot to open move picker
       - Picker shows: learnable moves, BP, accuracy, type, category
     (physical/special/status), description, secondary effects
       - Filter: All, Physical, Special, Status, STAB, Popular
       - Sorted by usage % when meta data available
       - Empty slot: dashed "Add move"
     - EVs (always visible):
       - Draggable bars with stat labels, EV value, calculated stat value
       - Color-coded per stat (HP red, Atk orange, Def yellow, SpA blue, SpD
     green, Spe pink)
       - Nature boost indicator: boosted stat label in green with "+", reduced
     stat label in red with "-"
       - Nature bump tick marks on the boosted stat's bar (shows EV breakpoints
     where +10% rounds up to an extra stat point)
       - Reduced stat bar dimmed (30% opacity)
       - Total EVs counter: "508 / 510 вҖў 2 remaining"
       - Preset buttons: Reset, Max Atk, Max Bulk
     - IVs (visible for formats that support them, hidden for Champions):
       - Shown alongside EVs вҖ” always visible, not collapsed
       - Default 31 all, editable per stat
     - Notes (per-Pokemon):
       - Collapsible text field below EVs
       - Freeform text for strategy notes

     Species Picker (inline, full-width)

     When the species picker is active (click species name в–ҫ or click "+" slot):
     - Right context panel hides
     - Picker takes the full width (minus dashboard sidebar + team strip)
     - Team strip stays visible at top, active slot shows "choosing..." state

     Layout: table left (52%) + detail right (48%)

     Left вҖ” Showdown-style data table:
     - Columns: sprite, Pokemon name, types, ability, HP, Atk, Def, SpA, SpD,
     Spe, BST, Usage %
     - Sortable columns (click header to sort)
     - Stat colors: green for high (120+), normal for mid, dimmed for low (<70)
     - Sticky header
     - Current Pokemon highlighted in teal
     - Selected/previewing Pokemon highlighted in blue
     - No row borders вҖ” hover background only (Tufte principle)

     Right вҖ” unique detail content (no duplication with table):
     - Key moves (not in the table)
     - Team fit analysis: +/- list showing how this Pokemon would affect your
     team's coverage, weaknesses, roles
     - VGC Pastes proven sets (when data available): player name, event,
     placement, full set with "Use this set" / "View full team" buttons
     - Action buttons: "Select with popular set", "Select blank"

     Search + filters (above the split):
     - Multi-field search bar: searches across species name, ability name, move
     name, type
     - Filter chips row 1: All (count), Top 20, Rising вҶ—, Niche
     - Filter chips row 2: Role в–ҫ (dropdown: Speed Control, Tailwind, Trick
     Room, Redirection, Fake Out, Intimidate, Priority, Weather Setter, Terrain
     Setter, Spread Damage, Setup Sweeper, Defensive Wall), Type в–ҫ, Learns Move
     в–ҫ, Stats в–ҫ
     - Auto-suggested team need filters (dashed teal border): "вңҰ Covers Ground",
      "вңҰ Covers Flying", "вңҰ Speed Control" вҖ” computed from current team's gaps
     - Cancel button returns to editor

     Context Panel (right 50%) вҖ” 3 Tabs

     Types tab:
     - No Pokemon selected (team overview): full 18-type defensive coverage
     matrix, color-coded (green=resist, red=weak, gray=neutral, italic=immune),
     warnings for uncovered types, offensive coverage summary
     - Pokemon selected: that Pokemon's individual type matchups, how tera type
     changes them, move coverage (what types your moves hit super-effectively)

     Speed tab:
     - No Pokemon selected (team overview): all 6 team members interleaved with
     meta Pokemon speed tiers, gap warnings
     - Pokemon selected: focused view вҖ” who you outspeed, who outspeeds you,
     with calculated speed values
     - V1 data source: base stats from @pkmn/dex with min/max/common speed
     benchmarks (0 EVs, 252 EVs, +nature, Choice Scarf, Tailwind). Meta pipeline
      data replaces these later.
     - Smart EV suggestions ("investing 20 EVs in Speed outspeeds 68% of meta
     Incineroar")

     Calc tab:
     - Uses @smogon/calc for damage calculations
     - Full field support: weather, terrain, screens, stat stages, abilities,
     Helping Hand
     - Smart auto-suggestions: offensive (your moves vs meta threats) +
     defensive (meta threats' attacks vs you)
     - Live recalculation when EVs/moves/items change
     - Manual calc mode available ("+ Manual Calc" button)
     - EV optimization insights ("shifting 28 EVs from SpD to Def survives
     Adamant Lando CC")

     Picker Behavior for Moves, Items, Abilities

     - Click field to open inline picker (replaces the field area, like
     Showdown)
     - Picker shows full list with descriptions inline:
       - Moves: name, type, category (P/S/Status), BP, accuracy, PP,
     description, secondary effects
       - Items: name, sprite, description/effect
       - Abilities: name, description, hidden ability indicator
     - Sorted by usage % when meta data available, alphabetical otherwise
     - Search/filter at top
     - Duplicate item warning (e.g., "Assault Vest already held by Urshifu")

     EV Nature Bump Indicators

     - On the stat with a positive nature boost (+10%): green tick marks appear
     above the EV bar at each breakpoint where the nature's rounding grants an
     extra stat point
     - Slider snaps to bump points when dragging near one (within 2 EVs)
     - Tooltip shows stat value + вҳ… when on a bump point
     - Only shown on the +nature stat

     Validation

     Three layers:
     1. Strip badges: red dot on Pokemon chips that have issues
     2. Inline field errors: red highlight on invalid fields with error text
     below
     3. Validation summary panel: triggered by "Validate" button in header,
     lists all issues across the team, click an issue to jump to the relevant
     Pokemon/field

     Mobile Layout

     - Dashboard sidebar hidden
     - Team strip: horizontal scroll
     - Editor: full-width, compact fields
     - Context panel: scrollable tabs below the editor (not side-by-side)
     - Species picker: full-screen, table stacks above detail

     Empty States

     - 0 Pokemon: workspace visible with empty strip (6 empty slots), editor
     area shows "Add your first Pokemon" button + "Import from Showdown paste"
     option
     - 1-5 Pokemon: normal editing, empty slots show "+" in strip
     - No team selected: teams list page

     ---
     Technical Architecture

     Packages & Dependencies

     Existing (reuse):
     - @pkmn/dex (0.10.7) вҖ” species, moves, abilities, items, natures, types
     - @pkmn/data (0.10.7) вҖ” raw data, generations API
     - @pkmn/sim (0.10.7) вҖ” format-specific TeamValidator
     - @pkmn/sets (5.2.0) вҖ” Showdown text parser (Teams.importTeam)
     - @pkmn/img (0.3.3) вҖ” sprite URLs
     - packages/pokemon вҖ” stat calculator, type effectiveness, team
     coverage/synergy, Showdown format conversion, format registry
     - packages/validators вҖ” team parsing, structure validation, format
     validation, profanity filter

     New dependency:
     - @smogon/calc вҖ” damage calculator engine (Gen 1-9, full field support)

     New Functions to Build

     Function: calculateNatureBumps()
     Package: @trainers/pokemon
     Purpose: For a given base stat + nature, return array of EV breakpoints
     where
       +nature grants an extra stat point
     в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ
     Function: calculateSpeedTiers()
     Package: @trainers/pokemon
     Purpose: Compare a Pokemon's speed against format benchmarks
       (min/max/scarf/tailwind)
     в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ
     Function: getSpeciesSearchIndex()
     Package: @trainers/pokemon
     Purpose: Build a searchable index of species by name, ability, move, type
     for
       the species picker
     в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ
     Function: calculateDamage()
     Package: apps/web (wrapper)
     Purpose: Wrapper around @smogon/calc that takes our PokemonSet types and
       returns formatted results

     Client-Side Calculations

     All analysis runs client-side for instant feedback:
     - Stat calculations (calculateStats)
     - Type coverage matrix (calculateTeamCoverage, getDefensiveMatchups)
     - Speed tier comparisons (calculateSpeedTiers)
     - Damage calculations (@smogon/calc)
     - Nature bump breakpoints (calculateNatureBumps)
     - Format validation (@pkmn/sim TeamValidator)

     @pkmn/dex data is already loaded client-side via the gen9 singleton.

     State Management

     - Server state: TanStack Query v5 for teams list, team data, meta stats
     (when available)
     - Editor form state: React state (no external form library needed вҖ” the
     editor is a custom UI, not a standard form). Derives from the saved team
     data, auto-saves via debounced mutation.
     - Auto-save: debounced Server Action (2s after last edit). Optimistic
     update via TanStack Query mutation. Shows "Saving..." вҶ’ "Saved" indicator.
     - Picker state: local React state (which picker is open, search query,
     filters, selected species)

     Routing

     /dashboard/alts/[handle]/teams          вҶ’ Teams list page
     /dashboard/alts/[handle]/teams/new      вҶ’ New team dialog
     /dashboard/alts/[handle]/teams/[id]     вҶ’ Team builder workspace
     /dashboard/alts/[handle]/teams/[id]/meta вҶ’ Meta page (future)

     ---
     Database Schema Changes

     Modified Tables

     pokemon table вҖ” add column:
     ALTER TABLE pokemon ADD COLUMN notes text;

     teams table вҖ” add column:
     ALTER TABLE teams ADD COLUMN parent_team_id bigint REFERENCES teams(id);
     ALTER TABLE teams ADD COLUMN format text;  -- if not already present

     New Tables (for meta pipeline вҖ” schema created in V1, populated later)

     -- External players from Limitless, RK9, Showdown (never auto-linked to 
     trainers.gg accounts)
     CREATE TABLE external_players (
       id bigint PRIMARY KEY GENERATED ALWAYS AS IDENTITY,
       source text NOT NULL CHECK (source IN ('limitless', 'rk9', 'showdown')),
       source_player_id text NOT NULL,
       display_name text NOT NULL,
       linked_alt_id bigint REFERENCES alts(id),
       linked_at timestamptz,
       linked_by text CHECK (linked_by IN ('self', 'admin')),
       created_at timestamptz DEFAULT now(),
       UNIQUE(source, source_player_id)
     );

     -- Raw tournament data imports
     CREATE TABLE data_imports (
       id bigint PRIMARY KEY GENERATED ALWAYS AS IDENTITY,
       source text NOT NULL CHECK (source IN ('native', 'limitless', 'rk9',
     'showdown')),
       external_ref text,
       format text NOT NULL,
       event_tier text CHECK (event_tier IN ('worlds', 'international',
     'regional', 'special_event', 'midseason_showdown', 'community', 'online')),
       imported_at timestamptz DEFAULT now()
     );

     -- Normalized team sheets from all sources
     CREATE TABLE imported_team_sheets (
       id bigint PRIMARY KEY GENERATED ALWAYS AS IDENTITY,
       import_id bigint NOT NULL REFERENCES data_imports(id),
       external_player_id bigint REFERENCES external_players(id),
       tournament_name text NOT NULL,
       format text NOT NULL,
       tournament_date date,
       player_count int,
       placement_tier text CHECK (placement_tier IN ('champion', 'finalist',
     'top4', 'top8', 'top16', 'top_cut', 'day2', 'completed')),
       position int NOT NULL CHECK (position BETWEEN 1 AND 6),
       species text NOT NULL,
       ability text NOT NULL,
       held_item text,
       tera_type text,
       move1 text, move2 text, move3 text, move4 text,
       -- Full data only from native tournaments or user opt-in
       nature text,
       ev_spread text,  -- stored as "252/4/0/0/252/0" for compact storage
       iv_spread text,
       created_at timestamptz DEFAULT now()
     );

     CREATE INDEX idx_imported_team_sheets_format_species ON
     imported_team_sheets(format, species);
     CREATE INDEX idx_imported_team_sheets_import_id ON
     imported_team_sheets(import_id);

     -- Aggregated meta snapshots (recomputed when new data arrives)
     CREATE TABLE format_meta_stats (
       id bigint PRIMARY KEY GENERATED ALWAYS AS IDENTITY,
       format text NOT NULL,
       computed_at timestamptz DEFAULT now(),
       period_start date NOT NULL,
       period_end date NOT NULL,
       total_teams int NOT NULL,
       total_tournaments int NOT NULL
     );

     -- Per-species usage stats per snapshot
     CREATE TABLE pokemon_usage_stats (
       id bigint PRIMARY KEY GENERATED ALWAYS AS IDENTITY,
       meta_id bigint NOT NULL REFERENCES format_meta_stats(id),
       species text NOT NULL,
       usage_pct numeric(5,2) NOT NULL,
       rank int NOT NULL,
       usage_change_7d numeric(5,2),
       usage_change_30d numeric(5,2),
       usage_pct_top_cut numeric(5,2),
       usage_pct_top8 numeric(5,2),
       conversion_rate numeric(4,2),  -- top_cut_usage / overall_usage
       sample_size int NOT NULL
     );

     CREATE INDEX idx_pokemon_usage_stats_meta ON pokemon_usage_stats(meta_id);
     CREATE INDEX idx_pokemon_usage_stats_species ON
     pokemon_usage_stats(species);

     -- Per-species detailed breakdowns (items, moves, spreads, teammates)
     CREATE TABLE pokemon_detail_stats (
       id bigint PRIMARY KEY GENERATED ALWAYS AS IDENTITY,
       meta_id bigint NOT NULL REFERENCES format_meta_stats(id),
       species text NOT NULL,
       items jsonb DEFAULT '[]',
       abilities jsonb DEFAULT '[]',
       moves jsonb DEFAULT '[]',
       spreads jsonb DEFAULT '[]',
       tera_types jsonb DEFAULT '[]',
       teammates jsonb DEFAULT '[]'
     );

     CREATE INDEX idx_pokemon_detail_stats_meta_species ON
     pokemon_detail_stats(meta_id, species);

     RLS Policies

     -- Teams: owner can CRUD, public teams readable by all
     -- Pokemon: readable if user owns the team or team is public
     -- External players: readable by all, writable by admin only
     -- Data imports: readable by all, writable by service role only
     -- Imported team sheets: readable by all
     -- Meta stats: readable by all, writable by service role only

     ---
     Data Pipeline Architecture (V1 = schema only, pipeline built later)

     Data Sources & Triggers

     Aggregation Flow (when pipeline is built)

     1. New data arrives (native tournament ends / webhook fires / scrape
     completes)
     2. Raw data inserted into data_imports + imported_team_sheets
     3. Edge function triggered: recomputes format_meta_stats +
     pokemon_usage_stats + pokemon_detail_stats for the affected format
     4. Uses sliding window (last 30 days) for "current meta"
     5. Old snapshot rows preserved for historical trend queries
     6. Cache tags busted вҶ’ UI picks up fresh data

     Weighted Meta Stats

     Usage stats weighted by event tier:
     - Worlds: 5x weight
     - International Championship: 3x weight
     - Regional: 2x weight
     - Special event / Midseason Showdown: 1.5x weight
     - Community / online: 1x weight

     Conversion rate: usage_pct_top_cut / usage_pct вҖ” values > 1.0 =
     overperforming, < 1.0 = overplayed

     Verification Plan

     Manual Testing

     1. Create a new team вҶ’ verify empty state shows prompts
     2. Add Pokemon via species picker вҶ’ verify smart filters, search, format
     legality
     3. Edit all fields (ability, item, nature, tera, moves, EVs, IVs, nickname,
      gender, shiny)
     4. Verify nature bump ticks on +nature stat EV bar
     5. Verify validation: duplicate items across team, illegal moves, EV
     overflow
     6. Verify per-Pokemon import/export (Showdown paste)
     7. Verify full team import (Showdown paste + Pokepaste URL)
     8. Verify full team export (clipboard, Pokepaste, shareable link)
     9. Verify fork creates full copy with parent_team_id
     10. Verify drag-and-drop reorder in strip
     11. Verify auto-save with debounce (edit вҶ’ wait 2s вҶ’ refresh вҶ’ changes
     persist)
     12. Verify Types tab: team overview + per-Pokemon view
     13. Verify Speed tab: speed tier comparisons with min/max/scarf/tailwind
     benchmarks
     14. Verify Calc tab: @smogon/calc integration with field conditions
     15. Verify format-aware behavior: VGC shows IVs, Champions hides IVs
     16. Verify mobile layout: horizontal strip, stacked editor + tabs
     17. Verify teams list: format filtering, grouping, default to active format
     18. Verify delete Pokemon вҶ’ empty slot
     19. Verify species change (click species name в–ҫ) вҶ’ picker opens вҶ’ select
     new species

     Automated Tests

     - Unit tests for calculateNatureBumps(), calculateSpeedTiers(),
     getSpeciesSearchIndex()
     - Unit tests for team CRUD Server Actions
     - Unit tests for validation logic (duplicate items, EV overflow, format
     legality)
     - Integration tests for auto-save flow
     - E2E test: create team вҶ’ add 6 Pokemon вҶ’ validate вҶ’ export as Showdown
     paste вҶ’ reimport вҶ’ verify identical
